<div id="review_323822826" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/323822826" />
    <a title="Wanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9246169-wanda"><img alt="Wanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528903039p2/9246169.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/323822826?book_show_action=true">May 04, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wanda" href="/user/show/9246169-wanda">Wanda</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=speculative-fiction">speculative-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=time-travel">time-travel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=reading-project">reading-project</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=read-in-2013">read-in-2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer323822826" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14542181602413647967">"Time Enough for Love follows Lazarus Long through a vast and magnificent timescape of centuries and worlds. Heinlein's longest and most ambitious work, it is the story of a man so in love with Life that he refused to stop living it."<br/><br/>I know that a lot of people love Heinlein and I have enjoyed a number of his novels too. This one, however, suffered from the need of editing--it was much too long and repetitious, especially if you have already read Stranger in a Strange Land or Friday. These books</span>
  <span id="freeText14542181602413647967" style="display:none">"Time Enough for Love follows Lazarus Long through a vast and magnificent timescape of centuries and worlds. Heinlein's longest and most ambitious work, it is the story of a man so in love with Life that he refused to stop living it."<br /><br />I know that a lot of people love Heinlein and I have enjoyed a number of his novels too. This one, however, suffered from the need of editing--it was much too long and repetitious, especially if you have already read Stranger in a Strange Land or Friday. These books make me wonder what kind of person RAH was and what it would have been like for his wife to live with him.<br /><br />He is a great proponent of being self-reliant--but the farther we get from the horse and plough, the more reliant we become on others to build our devices, be they mobile phones, computers or spaceships. We live in a society where we have to rely on others--I don't know how to make cloth or even how to turn cloth into clothes. Someone else does my farming, gardening and butchering and it will be that way until the replicators show up (and even then I'll be reliant on the replicator repairman!)<br /><br />RAH also seems to have some odd ideas about what women want (here's a clue, we don't necessarily want umpteen babies!). It seems like Lazarus Long always has some woman hanging onto his leg, begging to be impregnated. That got really old for me after the first time, let alone after the 20th time! Research has proven that when women get educated and have access to birth control, birth rates go down. We prefer to have fewer children and to invest more in those children, rather than produce dozens, and I'm sure women of the future, no matter how long they live, will continue to feel that way.<br /><br />Basically, I was irritated with the women characters for the duration of the book--they are not like any women that I know. In the end, I think they say much more about Heinlein that they do about humanity or our future.<br /><br /> <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14542181602413647967" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer42808346" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1838104859671311505">A number of fellow poly-folk and friends whom I respect highly had mentioned this book when discussing their awakening to their polyamourous natures, and so I decided to pick it up a while back. I'm normally a fairly fast reader, but this took me months to slog thru (with lots of breaks for other books). Heinlein's writing is difficult for me to read because I feel it's a bit convoluted and sometimes poorly executed, but he is a great storyteller, and while I can't say that I agree with all the </span>
  <span id="freeText1838104859671311505" style="display:none">A number of fellow poly-folk and friends whom I respect highly had mentioned this book when discussing their awakening to their polyamourous natures, and so I decided to pick it up a while back. I'm normally a fairly fast reader, but this took me months to slog thru (with lots of breaks for other books). Heinlein's writing is difficult for me to read because I feel it's a bit convoluted and sometimes poorly executed, but he is a great storyteller, and while I can't say that I agree with all the values espoused in his novels, I do think that in the long run, I understand why this book has been so influential on so many of the people I love and respect, and I enjoyed being given that insight.</span>

<div id="review_2061531431" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2061531431" />
    <a title="Joan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3837733-joan"><img alt="Joan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1278652944p2/3837733.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2061531431?book_show_action=true">Jul 18, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joan" href="/user/show/3837733-joan">Joan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780441810765" href="/book/show/6412752-time-enough-for-love">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3837733-joan?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3837733-joan?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3837733-joan?shelf=adult-books">adult-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3837733-joan?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2061531431&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2061531431" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1274990213396927137">I can't make up my mind on this one. Lets see if writing a review helps. <br/><br/>One of his themes is that any type of sex is ok, as long as no one is harmed by the action, which excuses a lot that many would find unacceptable such as statutory rape or incest, or when the story was published, homosexuality. His premise seems to be if they want it, they are old enough to enjoy it safely. I'm not necessarily so convinced of that. Kids may want it and think of nothing else. That doesn't mean they have the </span>
  <span id="freeText1274990213396927137" style="display:none">I can't make up my mind on this one. Lets see if writing a review helps. <br /><br />One of his themes is that any type of sex is ok, as long as no one is harmed by the action, which excuses a lot that many would find unacceptable such as statutory rape or incest, or when the story was published, homosexuality. His premise seems to be if they want it, they are old enough to enjoy it safely. I'm not necessarily so convinced of that. Kids may want it and think of nothing else. That doesn't mean they have the maturity to deal with sex. I agree that the reason for the taboo of incest is the problem of genetic nightmares resulting from the action and the way he wants to do it, does remove the problem. In his world, geneticists know enough to read the genetic code and be able to see if there are any bad results from the combination of the two codes. He spent a long time, many pages, explaining how two siblings could be completely unrelated genetically. It went over my head and I'm not able to judge whether his discussion has been overtaken by current technology or not. But I suspect he was trying to have his cake and eat it too in this section. History shows that incest does not have to be psychologically harmful. Take a look at the Egyptian Pharaohs. The majority of marriages were siblings. More likely half siblings but not necessarily. That civilization lasted much much longer than our current American civilization. However, I think in our culture, we are pretty far from being able to deal with incest, and I would not recommend it today. Interestingly enough, until the last part of the book, there really was not all that much sex. Once the family escaped to colonize a new planet, it did become pretty much a bacchanalia. He does a lot to prove his theme that sex can be a positive wonderful thing. A part that many forget is that Heinlein accepts the consequences of love and insists that the adults in a family all have a responsibility to take care of all the kids no mater what happens to some of the other adults and whether or not the kids were produced by other adults in this family. I can agree with this premise. <br /><br />There were a number of plot holes. Another problem were the enormous amount of space wasted on Lazarus's notebooks which are aphorisms galore. Many I don't agree with and none were fascinating reading. One of my objections was how did his family find Lazarus in time when he was dying in France in WWI at the end of the story. I find it objectionable that in the next several books in this series, people are rescued in a similar way: at the last moment, mostly because the family wants to do it rather than any reason involving a principle such as saving someone whose research is needed to keep civilization going. This ties in with one of my fundamental problems with Heinlein's philosophy: Heinlein's characters are allowed to do things other people can't do, fundamentally because they are not nearly as smart as Heinlein's characters. Intelligence is fine but does not guarantee ethical behavior. A genius can be a monster just as a stupid person can be a monster. Heinlein never admits that this is perfectly possible. <br /><br />I suppose I'll keep this book for now since I can't seem to make up my mind definitely whether to keep or toss. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1274990213396927137" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('GEhat58azX4aI4bN5JYNRRBPxyFK/tUHWQnKOUdhsa0xLu1/eILqX/OOqi+er1ZDTD0LN3AasnF/iDt9aZf99A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer1701811444519897459">Robert Anson Heinlein was an American novelist and science fiction writer. Often called "the dean of science fiction writers", he is one of the most popular, influential, and controversial authors of "hard science fiction". <br/><br/>He set a high standard for science and engineering plausibility and helped to raise the genre's standards of literary quality. He was the first SF writer to break into mainstre</span>
  <span id="freeText1701811444519897459" style="display:none">Robert Anson Heinlein was an American novelist and science fiction writer. Often called "the dean of science fiction writers", he is one of the most popular, influential, and controversial authors of "hard science fiction". <br /><br />He set a high standard for science and engineering plausibility and helped to raise the genre's standards of literary quality. He was the first SF writer to break into mainstream, general magazines such as <i>The Saturday Evening Post</i>, in the late 1940s. He was also among the first authors of bestselling, novel-length science fiction in the modern, mass-market era. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1701811444519897459" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
